to guard he ship he take with he only eighteen english and thirty symeron who not only serve as guide to show the way but as purveyor to procure provision they carry not only arrow for war but for hunting and fowl the head of which be proportion in size to the game which they be pursue : for oxen stag or wild boar they have arrow or javelin with head weigh a pound and half which they discharge near hand and which scarcely ever fail of be mortal the second sort be about half as heavy as the other and be generally shoot from they bow these be intend for smaller beast with the third sort of which the head be a ounce in weight they kill bird as this nation be in a state that do not set they above continual care for the immediate necessaries of life he that can temper iron best be among they most esteemed and perhaps it would be happy for every nation if honor and applause be as justly distribute and he be most distinguished whose ability be most useful to society how many chimerical title to precedence how many false pretence to respect would this rule bring to the ground every day by sunrise they begin to march and have travel till ten rest near some river till twelve then travel again till four they repose all night in house which the symeron have either leave standing in they former march or very readily erect for they by set up three or four post in the ground and lay pole from one to another in form of a roof which they thatch with palmetto bough and plantain leave in the valley where they be sheltered from the wind they leave three or four foot below open but on the hill where they be more expose to the chill blast of the night they thatch they close to the ground leave only a door for entrance and a vent in the middle of the room for the smoke of three fire which they make in every house in they march they meet not only with plenty of fruit upon the bank of the river but with wild swine in great abundance of which the symeron without difficulty kill for the most part as much as be want one day however they find a otter and be about to dress it at which drake express he wonder be ask by pedro the chief symeron : be you a man of war and in want and yet doubt whether this be meat that have blood in it for which drake in private rebuke he say the relater whether justly or not it be not very important to determine there seem to be in drake 's scruple somewhat of superstition perhaps not easily to be justified and the negro 's answer be at least martial and will i believe be generally acknowledge to be rational on the third day of they march feb 6 they come to a town of the symeron situate on the side of a hill and encompass with a ditch and a mudwall to secure it from a sudden surprise : here they live with great neatness and plenty and some observation of religion pay great reverence to the cross a practice which drake prevail upon they to change for the use of the lord 's prayer here they importune drake to stay for a few day promise to double he strength but he either think greater number unnecessary or fear that if any difference should arise he should be overborne by the number of symeron or that they would demand to share the plunder that should be take in common or for some other reason that might easily occur refuse any addition to he troop endeavor to express he refusal in such term as might heighten they opinion of he bravery he then proceed on he journey through cool shades and lofty wood which sheltered they so effectually from the sun that they march be less toilsome than if they have travel in england during the heat of the summer four of the symeron that be acquaint with the way go about a mile before the troop and scatter branch to direct they then follow twelve symeron after whom come the english with the two leader and the other symeron close the rear on February 11 they arrive at the top of a very high hill on the summit of which grow a tree of wonderful greatness in which they have cut step for the more easy ascent to the top where there be a kind of tower to which they invite drake and from thence show he not only the north sea from whence they come but the great south sea on which no english vessel have ever sail this prospect exciting he natural curiosity and ardor for adventure and discovery he lift up he hand to god and implore he blessing upon the resolution which he then form of sailing in a english ship on that sea then continue they march they come after two day into a open level country where they passage be somewhat incommoded with the grass which be of a peculiar kind consist of a stalk like that of wheat and a blade on which the ox and other cattle feed till it grow too high for they to reach then the inhabitant set it on fire and in three day it spring up again this they be oblige to do thrice a year so great be the fertility of the soil at length be within view of panama they leave all frequented road for fear of be discover and post themselves in a grove near the way between panama and nombre de dios then they send a symeron in the habit of a negro of panama to inquire on what night the reco or driver of mule by which the treasure be carry be to set forth the messenger be so well qualify for he undertaking and so industrious in the prosecution of it that he soon return with a account that the treasurer of lima intend to return to europe would pass that night with eight mule laden with gold and one with jewel have receive this information they immediately march towards venta cruz the first town on the way to nombre de dios send for security two symeron before who as they go perceive by the scent of a match that some spaniard be before they and go silently forward surprise a soldier asleep upon the ground they immediately bind he and bring he to drake who upon inquiry find that they spy have not deceive they in he intelligence the soldier have inform himself of the captain 's name conceive such a confidence in he well known clemency that after have make a ample discovery of the treasure that be now at hand he petition not only that he would command the symeron to spare he life but that when the treasure should fall into he hand he would allow he as much as might maintain he and he mistress since they be about to gain more than they whole company could carry drake then order he man to lie down in the long grass about fifty pace from the road half on one side with himself and half on the other with oxenham and the captain of the symeron so much behind that one company might seize the foremost recoe and the other the hindermost for the mule of these reco or driver be tie together travel on a line and be all guide by lead the first when they have lie about a hour in this place they begin to hear the bell of the mule on each hand upon which order be give that the drive which come from venta cruz should pass unmolested because they carry nothing of great value and those only be intercept which be travel thither and that none of the man should rise up till the signal should be give but one robert pike heat with strong liquor leave he company and prevail upon one of the symeron to creep with he to the wayside that they might signalize themselves by seize the first mule and hear the trampling of a horse as he lay could not be restrain by the symeron from rise up to observe who be pass by this he do so imprudently that he be discover by the passenger for by drake 's order the english have put they shirt on over they coat that the night and tumult might not hinder they from know one another the gentleman be immediately observe by drake to change he trot into a gallop but the reason of it not appear it be imputed to he fear of the robber that usually infest that road and the english still continue to expect the treasure in a short time one of the reco that be pass towards venta cruz come up and be eagerly seize by the english who expect nothing less than half the revenue of the indy nor be it easy to imagine they mortification and perplexity when they find only two mule laden with silver the rest have no other burden than provision the driver be bring immediately to the captain and inform he that the horseman whom he have observe pass by with so much precipitation have inform the treasurer of what he have observe and advise he to send back the mule that carry he gold and jewel and suffer only the rest to proceed that he might by that cheap experiment discover whether there be any ambush on the way that drake be not less disgusted than he follower at the disappointment can not be doubt but there be now no time to be spend in complaint the whole country be alarm and all the force of the spaniard be summon to overwhelm he he have no fortress to retire to every man be he enemy and every retreat better know to the spaniard than to himself this be a occasion that demand all the quality of a hero a intrepidity never to be shake and a judgment never to be perplexed he immediately consider all the circumstance of he present situation and find that it afford he only the choice of march back the same way through which he come or of force he passage to venta cruz to march back be to confess the superiority of he enemy and to animate they to the pursuit the wood would afford opportunity of ambush and he follower must often disperse themselves in search of provision who would become a easy prey dispirit by they disappointment and fatigue by they march on the way to venta cruz he should have nothing to fear but from open attack and expect enemy determine therefore to pass forward to venta cruz he ask pedro the leader of the symeron whether he be resolve to follow he and have receive from he the strongest assurance that nothing should separate they command he man to refresh themselves and prepare to set forward when they come within a mile of the town they dismiss the mule which they have make use of for they more easy and speedy passage and continue they march along a road cut through thick wood in which a company of soldier who be quarter in the place to defend it against the symeron have post themselves together with a convent of friar head by one of they brethren whose zeal against the northern heresy have incite he to hazard he person and assume the province of a general drake who be advertise by two symeron whom he send before of the approach of the spaniard command he follower to receive the first volley without firing in a short time he hear himself summon by the spanish captain to yield with a promise of protection and kind treatment to which he answer with defiance contempt and the discharge of he pistol immediately the spaniard pour in they shoot by which only one man be kill and drake with some other slightly wound upon which the signal be give by drake 's whistle to fall upon they the english after discharge they arrow and shoot press furiously forward and drive the spaniard before they which the symeron whom the terror of the shot have drive to some distance observe and recall they courage animated each other with song in they own language and rush forward with such impetuosity that they overtake they near the town and support by the english disperse they with the loss of only one man who after he have receive he wound have strength and resolution leave to kill he assailant they pursue the enemy into the town in which they meet with some plunder which be give to the symeron and treat the inhabitant with great clemency drake himself go to the spanish lady to assure they that no injury should be offer they so inseparable be humanity from true courage have thus break the spirit and scatter the force of the spaniard he pursue he march to he ship without any apprehension of danger yet with great speed be very solicitous about the state of the crew so that he allow he man harass as they be but little time for sleep or refreshment but by kind exhortation gentle authority and a cheerful participation of all they hardship prevail upon they to bear without murmur not only the toil of travel but on some day the pain of hunger in this march he owe much of he expedition to the assistance of the symeron who be accustom to the climate and naturally robust not only bring he intelligence and show the way but carry necessaries provide victuals and build lodgings and when any of the english faint in the way two of they would carry he between they for two mile together nor be they valor less than they industry after they have learn from they english companion to despise the firearm of the spaniard when they be within five league of the ship they find a town build in they absence by the symeron at which drake consent to halt send a symeron to the ship with he gold toothpick as a token which though the master know it be not sufficient to gain the messenger credit till upon examination he find that the captain have order he to regard no messenger without he handwriting have engraven he name upon it with the point of he knife he then send the pinnace up the river which they meet and afterwards send to the town for those whose weariness have make they unable to march further on February 23 the whole company be reunite and drake whose good or ill success never prevail over he piety celebrate they meeting with thanks to god drake not yet discourage now turn he thought to new prospects and without languish in melancholy reflection upon he past miscarriage employ himself in form scheme for repair they eager of action and acquaint with man 's nature he never suffer idleness to infect he follower with cowardice but keep they from sink under any disappointment by divert they attention to some new enterprise upon consultation with he own man and the symeron he find they divide in they opinion some declare that before they engage in any new attempt it be necessary to increase they store of provision and other urge that the ship in which the treasure be convey should be immediately attack the symeron propose a third plan and advise he to undertake another march over land to the house of one pezoro near veragua whose slave bring he every day more than two hundred pound sterling from the mine which he heap together in a strong stone house which might by the help of the english be easily force drake be unwilling to fatigue he follower with another journey determine to comply with both the other opinion and man he two pinnace the bear and the minion he send john oxenham in the bear towards tolu to seize upon provision and go himself in the minion to the cabeza to intercept the treasure that be to be transport from veragua and that coast to the fleet at nombre de dios first dismiss with present those symeron that desire to return to they wife and order those that choose to remain to be entertain in the ship drake take at the cabeza a frigate of nicaragua the pilot of which inform he that there be in the harbor of veragua a ship freight with more than a million of gold to which he offer to conduct he be well acquaint with the sounding if he might be allow he share of the prize so much be he avarice superior to he honesty drake after some deliberation comply with the pilot 's importunity sail towards the harbor but have no sooner enter the mouth of it than he hear the report of artillery which be answer by other at a greater distance upon which the pilot tell he that they wero discover this be the signal appoint by the governor to alarm the coast drake now think it convenient to return to the ship that he might inquire the success of the other pinnace which he find with a frigate that she have take with twenty-eight fat hog two hundred hen and great store of maize or indian corn the vessel itself be so strong and well build that he fit it out for war determine to attack the fleet at nombre de dios on march the 21st he set sail with the new frigate and the bear towards the cabeza at which he arrive in about two day and find there ttu a frenchman with a ship of war who after have receive from he a supply of water and other necessaries entreat that he might join with he in he attempt which drake consent to admit he to accompany he with twenty of he man stipulate to allow they a equal share of whatever booty they should gain yet be they not without some suspicion of danger from this new ally he have eighty man and they be now reduce to thirty-one then man the frigate and two pinnace they set sail for the cabeza where they leave the frigate which be too large for the shallows over which they be to pass and proceed to rio francisco here they land and have order the pinnace to return to the same place on the fourth day follow travel through the wood towards nombre de dios with such silence and regularity as surprised the french who do not imagine the symeron so discreet or obedient as they appear and be therefore in perpetual anxiety about the fidelity of they guide and the probability of they return nor do the symeron treat they with that submission and regard which they pay to the english whose bravery and conduct they have already try at length after a laborious march of more than seven league they begin to hear the hammer of the carpenter in the bay it be the custom in that hot season to work in the night and in a short time they perceive the approach of the reco or drove of mule from panama they now no longer doubt that they labor would be reward and every man imagine himself secure from poverty and labor for the remain part of he life they therefore when the mule come up rush out and seize they with a alacrity proportion to they expectation the three drove consist of one hundred and nine mule each of which carry three hundred pound ' weight of silver it be to little purpose that the soldier order to guard the treasure attempt resistance after a short combat in which the french captain and one of the symeron be wound it appear with how much greater ardor man be animated by interest than fidelity as it be possible for they to carry away but a small part of this treasure after have weary themselves with hide it in hole and shallow water they determine to return by the same way and without be pursue enter the wood where the french captain be disable by he wound be oblige to stay two of he company continue with he when they have go forward about two league the frenchman miss another of they company who upon inquiry be know to be intoxicate with wine and suppose to have lose himself in the wood by neglect to observe the guide but common prudence not allow they to hazard the whole company by too much solicitude for a single life they travel on towards rio francisco at which they arrive April the 3rd but look out for they pinnace be surprise with the sight of seven spanish shallop and immediately conclude that some intelligence of they motion have be carry to nombre de dios and that these vessel have be fit out to pursue they which might undoubtedly have overpower the pinnace and they feeble crew nor do they suspicion stop here but immediately it occur to they that they man have be compel by torture to discover where they frigate and ship be station which be weakly man and without the presence of the chief commander would fall into they hand almost without resistance and all possibility of escape be entirely cut off these reflection sink the whole company into despair and every one instead of endeavor to break through the difficulty that surround he resign up himself to he ill fortune when drake whose intrepidity be never to be shake and whose reason be never to be surprised or embarrassed represent to they that though the spaniard should have make themselves master of they pinnace they might yet be hinder from discover the ship he put they in mind that the pinnace could not be take the man examine they examination compare the resolution form they vessel send out and the ship take in a instant some time must necessarily be spend before the last blow could be strike and if that time be not negligently lose it might be possible for some of they to reach the ship before the enemy and direct they to change they station they be animated with this discourse by which they discover that they leader be not without hope but when they come to look more nearly into they situation they be unable to conceive upon what it be found to pass by land be impossible as the way lay over high mountain through thick wood and deep river and they have not a single boat in they power so that a passage by water seem equally impracticable but drake whose penetration immediately discover all the circumstance and inconveniency of every scheme soon determine upon the only means of success which they condition afford they and order he man to make a raft out of the tree that be then float on the river offer himself to put off to sea upon it and cheerfully ask who would accompany he john owen john smith and two frenchman who be willing to share he fortune embark with he on the raft which be fit out with a sail make of a biscuit-sack and a oar to direct its course instead of a rudder then have comfort the rest with assurance of he regard for they and resolution to leave nothing unattempted for they deliverance he put off and after have with much difficulty sail three league descry two pinnace hast towards he which upon a nearer approach he discover to be he own and perceive that they anchor behind a point that jut out into the sea he put to shore and cross the land on foot be receive by he company with that satisfaction which be only know to those that have be acquaint with danger and distress the same night they row to rio francisco where they take in the rest with what treasure they have be able to carry with they through the wood then sail back with the utmost expedition they return to they frigate and soon after to they ship where drake divide the gold and silver equally between the french and the english here they spend about fourteen day in fitting out they frigate more completely and then dismiss the spaniard with they ship lay a few day among the cabeza while twelve english and sixteen symeron travel once more into the country as well to recover the french captain whom they have leave wound as to bring away the treasure which they have hide in the sand drake whom he company would not suffer to hazard he person in another land expedition go with they to rio francisco where he find one of the frenchman who have stay to attend they captain and be inform by he upon he inquiry after he fortune that half a hour after they separation the spaniards come upon they and easily seize upon the wound captain but that he companion might have escape with he have he not prefer money to life for see he throw down a box of jewel that retard he he could not forbear take it up and with that and the gold which he have already be so loaded that he could not escape with regard to the bar of gold and silver which they have conceal in the ground he inform they that two thousand man have be employ in digging for they the man however either mistrust the informer 's veracity or confident that what they have hide could not be find pursue they journey but upon they arrival at the place find the ground turn up for two mile round and be able to recover no more than thirteen bar ' of silver and a small quantity of gold they discover afterwards that the frenchman who be leave in the wood fall afterwards into the hand of the spaniard be tortured by they till he confess where drake have conceal he plunder so fatal to drake 's expedition be the drunkenness of he follower then dismiss the french they pass by carthagena with they color fly and soon after take a frigate laden with provision and honey which they value as a great restorative and then sail away to the cabeza here they stay about a week to clean they vessel and fit they for a long voyage determine to set sail for england and that the faithful symeron might not go away unrewarded break up they pinnace and give they the iron the most valuable present in the world to a nation whose only employment be war and hunting and amongst whom show and luxury have no place pedro they captain be desire by drake to go through the ship and to choose what he most desire fix he eye upon a cimetar set with diamond which the french captain have present to drake and be unwilling to ask for so valuable a present offer for it four large quoit or thick plate of gold which he have hitherto conceal but drake desirous to show he that fidelity be seldom without a recompense give it he with the highest profession of satisfaction and esteem pedro receive it with the utmost gratitude inform he that by bestow it he have confer greatness and honor upon he for by present it to he king he doubt not of obtain the highest rank amongst the symeron he then persist in he resolution of leave the gold which be generously throw by drake into the common stock for he say that those at whose expense he have be send out ought to share in all the gain of the expedition whatever pretence cavil and chicanery might supply for the appropriation of any part of it thus be drake 's character consistent with itself he be equally superior to avarice and fear and through whatever danger he might go in quest of gold he think it not valuable enough to be obtain by artifice or dishonesty they now forsake the coast of america which for many month they have keep in perpetual alarm have take more than two hundred ship of all size between carthagena and nombre de dios of which they never destroy any unless they be fit out against they nor ever detain the prisoner longer than be necessary for they own security or concealment provide for they in the same manner as for themselves and protect they from the malice of the symerous a behavior which humanity dictate and which perhaps even policy can not disapprove he must certainly meet with obstinate opposition who make it equally dangerous to yield as to resist and who leave he enemy no hope but from victory what riches they acquire be not particularly related but it be not to be doubt that the plunder of so many vessel together with the silver which they seize at nombre de dios must amount to a very large sum though the part that be allot to drake be not sufficient to lull he in effeminacy or to repress he natural inclination to adventure they arrive at plymouth on the 9th of August 1573 on Sunday in the afternoon and so much be the people delighted with the news of they arrival that they leave the preacher and run in crowd to the quay with shout and congratulation drake have in he former expedition have a view of the south sea and form a resolution to sail upon it do not suffer himself to be divert from he design by the prospect of any difficulty that might obstruct the attempt nor any danger that might attend the execution obstacle which brave man often find it much more easy to overcome than secret envy and domestick treachery drake 's reputation be now sufficiently advance to incite detraction and opposition and it be easy to imagine that a man by nature superior to mean artifice and breed from he earliest year to the labor and hardship of a sea-life be very little acquaint with policy and intrigue very little verse in the method of application to the powerful and great and unable to obviate the practice of those whom he merit have make he enemy nor be such the only opponent of great enterprise : there be some man of narrow view and grovel conception who without the instigation of personal malice treat every new attempt as wild and chimerical and look upon every endeavor to depart from the beaten track as the rash effort of a warm imagination or the glitter speculation of a exalted mind that may please and dazzle for a time but can produce no real or lasting advantage these man value themselves upon a perpetual skepticism upon believe nothing but they own sens upon call for demonstration where it can not possibly be obtain and sometimes upon hold out against it when it be lay before they upon invent argument against the success of any new undertaking and where argument can not be find upon treat it with contempt and ridicule such have be the most formidable enemy of the great benefactor to mankind and to these we can hardly doubt but that much of the opposition which drake meet with be to be attribute for they notion and discourse be so agreeable to the lazy the envious and the timorous that they seldom fail of become popular and direct the opinion of mankind whatsoever be he obstacle and whatsoever the motive that produce they it be not till the year 1577 that he be able to assemble a force proportion to he design and to obtain a commission from the queen by which he be constitute captain-general of a fleet consist of five vessel of which the pelican admiral of a hundred ton be command by himself the elizabeth viceadmiral of eighty ton by john winter the marigold of thirty ton by john thoma the swan fifty ton by john chester the christopher of fifteen ton by thoma moche the same as it seem who be carpenter in the former voyage and destroy one of the ship by drake 's direction these ship equip partly by himself and partly by other private adventurer he man with one hundred and sixty-four stout sailor and furnish with such provision as he judge necessary for the long voyage in which he be engage nor do he confine he concern to naval store or military preparation but carry with he whatever he think might contribute to raise in those nation with which he should have any intercourse the highest idea of the politeness and magnificence of he native country he therefore not only procure a complete service of silver for he own table and furnish the cook-room with many vessel of the same metal but engage several musician to accompany he rightly judge that nothing would more excite the admiration of any savage and uncivilized people have be drive back by a tempest in they first attempt and oblige to return to plymouth to repair the damages which they have suffer they set sail again from thence on the 13th of December 1577 and on the 25th have sight of cape cantin in barbary from whence they coast on southward to the island of mogador which drake have appoint for the first place of rendezvous and on the 27th bring the whole fleet to anchor in a harbor on the mainland they be soon after they arrival discover by the moor that inhabit those coast who send two of the principal man amongst they on board drake 's ship receive at the same time two of he company as hostage these man he not only treat in the most splendid manner but present with such thing as they appear most to admire it be with he a established maxim to endeavor to secure in every country a kind reception to such englishman as might come after he by treat the inhabitant with kindness and generosity a conduct at once just and politick to the neglect of which may be attribute many of the injury suffer by we sailor in distant country which be generally ascribe rather to the effect of wickedness and folly of we own commander than the barbarity of the native who seldom fall upon any unless they have be first plunder or insult and in reveng the ravages of one crew upon another of the same nation be guilty of nothing but what be countenance by the example of the european themselves but this friendly intercourse be in appearance soon break for on the next day observe the moor make signal from the land they send out they boat as before to fetch they to the ship and one john fry leap ashore intend to become a hostage as on the former day when immediately he be seize by the moor and the crew observe great number to start up from behind the rock with weapon in they hand find it madness to attempt he rescue and therefore provide for they own security by return to the ship fry be immediately carry to the king who be then in continual expectation of a invasion from portugal suspect that these ship be send only to observe the coast and discover a proper harbor for the main fleet but be inform who they be and whither they be bind not only dismiss he captive but make large offer of friendship and assistance which drake however do not stay to receive but be disgust at this breach of the law of commerce and afraid of further violence after have spend some day in search for he man in which he meet with no resistance leave the coast on December 31 some time before fry 's return who be oblige by this accident to somewhat a longer residence among the moor be afterwards send home in a merchant 's ship on January 16 they arrive at cape blanc have in they passage take several spanish vessel here while drake be employ he man in catch fish of which this coast afford great plenty and various kind the inhabitant come down to the seaside with they alisorge or leather bottle to traffick for water which they be willing to purchase with ambergris and other gum but drake compassionate the misery of they condition give they water whenever they ask for it and leave they they commodity to traffick with when they should be again reduce to the same distress without find the same generosity to relieve they here have discharge some spanish ship which they have take they set sail towards the isle of cape verd and on January 28 come to anchor before mayo hope to furnish themselves with fresh water but have land they find the town by the waterside entirely desert and march further up the country see the valley extremely fruitful and abound with ripe fig cocoa and plantain but could by no means prevail upon the inhabitant to converse or traffick with they however they be suffer by they to range the country without molestation but find no water except at such a distance from the sea that the labor of convey it to the ship be greater than it be at that time necessary for they to undergo salt have they want it might have be obtain with less trouble be leave by the sea upon the sand and harden by the sun during the ebb in such quantity that the chief traffick of they island be carry on with it January 31 they pass by st jago a island at that time divide between the native and the portuguese who first enter these island under the show of traffick by degree establish themselves -- claim a superiority over the original inhabitant and harass they with such cruelty that they oblige they either to fly to the wood and mountain and perish with hunger or to take up arm against they oppressor and under the insuperable disadvantage with which they contend to die almost without a battle in defense of they natural rights and ancient possession such treatment have the native of st jago receive which have drive they into the rocky part of the island from whence they make incursion into the plantation of the portuguese sometimes with loss but generally with that success which desperation naturally procure so that the portuguese be in continual alarm and live with the natural consequence of guilt terror and anxiety they be wealthy but not happy and possess the island but not enjoy it they then sail on within sight of fuego a island so call from a mountain about the middle of it continually burn and like the rest inhabit by the portuguese two league to the south of which lie brava which have receive its name from its fertility abound though uninhabited with all kind of fruit and water with great number of spring and brook which would easily invite the possessor of the adjacent island to settle in it but that it afford neither harbor nor anchorage drake after have send out he boat with plummet be not able to find any ground about it and it be report that many experiment have be make with the same success however he take in water sufficient and on the 2nd of February set sail for the strait of magellan on February 17 they pass the equator and continue they voyage with sometimes calm and sometimes contrary wind but without any memorable accident to march 28 when one of they vessel with twenty-eight man and the greatest part of they fresh water on board be to they great discouragement separate from they but they perplexity last not long for on the next day they discover and rejoin they associate in they long course which give they opportunity of observe several animal both in the air and water at that time very little known nothing entertain or surprise they more than the fly fish which be near of the same size with a herr and have fin of the length of he whole body by the help of which when he be pursue by the bonito or great mackerel as soon as he find himself upon the point of be take he spring up into the air and fly forward as long as he wing continue wet moisture be as it seem necessary to make they pliant and moveable and when they become dry and stiff he fall down into the water unless some bark or ship intercept he and dip they again for a second flight this unhappy animal be not only pursue by fish in he natural element but attack in the air where he hope for security by the don or sparkite a great bird that prey upon fish and they species must surely be destroy be not they increase so great that the young fry in one part of the year cover the sea there be another fish name the cuttle of which whole shoal will sometimes rise at once out of the water and of which a great multitude fall into they ship at length have sail without sight of land for sixty-three day they arrive April 5 at the coast of brasil where on the 7th the christopher be separate again from they by a storm after which they sail near the land to the southward and on the 14th anchor under a cape which they afterwards call cape joy because in two day the vessel which they have lose return to they have spend a fortnight in the river of pla to refresh he man after they long voyage and then stand out to sea he be again surprise by a sudden storm in which they lose sight of the swan this accident determine drake to contract the number of he fleet that he might not only avoid the inconvenience of such frequent separation but ease the labor of he man by have more hand in each vessel for this purpose he sail along the coast in quest of a commodious harbor and on may 13 discover a bay which seem not improper for they purpose but which they dare not enter till it be examine a employment in which drake never trust any whatever might be he confidence in he follower on other occasion he well know how fatal one moment 's inattention might be and how easily almost every man suffer himself to be surprise by indolence and security he know the same credulity that might prevail upon he to trust another might induce another to commit the same office to a third and it must be at length that some of they would be deceive he therefore as at other time order the boat to be hoist out and take the line into he hand go on sound the passage till he be three league from he ship when on a sudden the weather change the sky blacken the wind whistle and all the usual forerunner of a storm begin to threaten they nothing be now desire but to return to the ship but the thickness of the fog intercept it from they sight make the attempt little other than desperate by so many unforeseen accident be prudence itself liable to be embarrass so difficult be it sometimes for the quickest sagacity and most enlighten experience to judge what measure ought to be take to trust another to sound a unknown coast appear to drake folly and presumption to be absent from he fleet though but for a hour prove nothing less than to hazard the success of all they labor hardship and danger in this perplexity which drake be not more sensible of than those whom he have leave in the ship nothing be to be omit however dangerous that might contribute to extricate they from it as they could venture nothing of equal value with the life of they general captain thoma therefore have the lightest vessel steer boldly into the bay and take the general aboard drop anchor and lay out of danger while the rest that be in the open sea suffer much from the tempest and the mary a portuguese prize be drive away before the wind the other as soon as the tempest be over discover by the fire which be make on shore where drake be repair to he here go on shore they meet with no inhabitant though there be several house or hut stand in which they find a good quantity of dry fowl and among they a great number of ostrich of which the thigh be as large as those of a sheep these bird be too heavy and unwieldy to rise from the ground but with the help of they wing run so swiftly that the english could never come near enough to shoot at they the indian commonly by hold a large plume of feather before they and walk gently forward drive the ostrich into some narrow neck or point of land then spread a strong net from one side to the other to hinder they from return back to the open field set they dog upon they thus confine between the net and the water and when they be throw on they back rush in and take they not find this harbor convenient or well store with wood and water they leave it on the 15th of may and on the 18th enter another much safer and more commodious which they no sooner arrive at than drake whose restless application never remit send winter to the southward in quest of those ship which be absent and immediately after sail himself to the northward and happily meeting with the swan conduct it to the rest of the fleet after which in pursuance of he former resolution he order it to be break up reserve the iron-work for a future supply the other vessel which they lose in the late storm could not be discover while they be thus employ upon a island about a mile from the mainland to which at low water there be a passage on foot they be discover by the native who appear upon a hill at a distance dancing and hold up they hand as beckon the english to they which drake observe send out a boat with knife bell and bugle and such thing as by they usefulness or novelty he imagine would be agreeable as soon as the english land they observe two man run towards they as depute by the company who come within a little distance and then stand still could not be prevail upon to come nearer the english therefore tie they present to a pole which they fix in the ground and then retire see the indian advance who take what they find upon the pole leave in return such feather as they wear upon they head with a small bone about six inch in length carve round the top and burnished drake observe they inclination to friendship and traffick advance with some of he company towards the hill upon sight of whom the indian range themselves in a line from east to west and one of they run from one end of the rank to the other backwards and forwards bow himself towards the rise and set of the sun hold he hand over he head and frequently stop in the middle of the rank leap up towards the moon which then shine directly over they head thus call the sun and moon the deity they worship to witness the sincerity of they profession of peace and friendship while this ceremony be perform drake and he company ascend the hill to the apparent terror of the indian whose apprehension when the english perceive they peaceably retire which give the native so much encouragement that they come forward immediately and exchange they arrow feather and bone for such trifle as be offer they thus they trade for some time but by frequent intercourse finding that no violence be intend they become familiar and mingled with the english without the least distrust they go quite naked except a skin of some animal which they throw over they shoulder when they lie in the open air they knit up they hair which be very long with a roll of ostrich feather and usually carry they arrow wrap up brit that they may not encumber they they be make with reed head with flint and therefore not heavy they bow be about a ell long they chief ornament be paint which they use of several kind delineate generally upon they body the figure of the sun and moon in honor of they deity it be observable that most nation amongst whom the use of clothes be unknown paint they body such be the practice of the first inhabitant of we own country from this custom do we earliest enemy the pict owe they denomination as it be not probable that caprice or fancy should be uniform there must be doubtless some reason for a practice so general and prevail in distant part of the world which have no communication with each other the original end of paint they body be probably to exclude the cold a end which if we believe some relation be so effectually produce by it that the man thus paint never shiver at the most piercing blast but doubtless any people so harden by continual severity would even without paint be less sensible of the cold than the civilized inhabitant of the same climate however this practice may contribute in some degree to defend they from the injury of winter and in those climate where little evaporate by the pore may be use with no great inconvenience but in hot country where perspiration in greater degree be necessary the native only use unction to preserve they from the other extreme of weather : so well do either reason or experience supply the place of science in savage country they have no canoe like the other indian nor any method of cross the water which be probably the reason why the bird in the adjacent island be so tame that they might be take with the hand have never be before fright or molest the great plenty of fowl and seal which crowd the shallows in such number that they kill at they first arrival two hundred of they in a hour contribute much to the refreshment of the english who name the place seal bay from that animal these seal seem to be the chief food of the native for the english often find raw piece of they flesh half eat and leave as they suppose after a full meal by the indian whom they never know to make use of fire or any art in dress or prepare they victuals nor be they other custom less wild or uncouth than they way of feed one of they have receive a cap off the general 's head and be extremely pleased as well with the honor as the gift to express he gratitude and confirm the alliance between they retire to a little distance and thrust a arrow into he leg let the blood run upon the ground testify as it be probable that he value drake 's friendship above life have stay fifteen day among these friendly savage in 47 deg 30 min s lat on June 3 they set sail towards the south sea and six day afterwards stop at another little bay to break up the christopher then pass on they cast anchor in another bay not more than twenty league distant from the strait of magellan it be now time seriously to deliberate in what manner they should act with regard to the portuguese prize which have be separate from they by the storm have not yet rejoin they to return in search of it be sufficiently mortifying to proceed without it be not only to deprive themselves of a considerable part of they force but to expose they friend and companion whom common hardship and danger have endear to they to certain death or captivity this consideration prevail and therefore on the 18th after prayer to god with which drake never forget to begin a enterprise he put to sea and the next day near port julian discover they associate whose ship be now grow leaky have suffer much both in the first storm by which they be disperse and afterwards in fruitless attempt to regain the fleet drake therefore be desirous to relieve they fatigue enter port julian and as it be he custom always to attend in person when any important business be in hand go ashore with some of the chief of he company to seek for water where he be immediately accost by two native of whom magellan leave a very terrible account have describe they as a nation of giant and monster nor be he narrative entirely without foundation for they be of the largest size though not taller than some englishman they strength be proportion to they bulk and they voice loud boisterous and terrible what be they manners before the arrival of the spaniard it be not possible to discover but the slaughter make of they countryman perhaps without provocation by these cruel intruder and the general massacre with which that part of the world have be depopulate might have raise in they a suspicion of all stranger and by consequence make they inhospitable treacherous and bloody the two who associate themselves with the english appear much pleased with they new guest receive willingly what be give they and very exactly observe every thing that pass seem more particularly delighted with see oliver the master-gunner shoot a english arrow they shoot themselves likewise in emulation but they arrow always fall to the ground far short of he soon after this friendly contest come another who observe the familiarity of he countryman with the stranger appear much displeased and as the englishman perceive endeavor to dissuade they from such a intercourse what effect he argument have be soon after apparent for another of drake 's companion be desirous to show the third indian a specimen of the english valor and dexterity attempt likewise to shoot a arrow but draw it with he full force burst the bowstr upon which the indian who be unacquainted with they other weapon imagine he disarm follow the company as they be walk negligently down towards they boat and let fly they arrow aim particularly at winter who have the bow in he hand he find himself wound in the shoulder endeavor to refit he bow and turn about be pierce with a second arrow in the breast oliver the gunner immediately present he piece at the insidious assailant which fail to take fire give they time to level another flight of arrow by which he be kill nor perhaps have any of they escape surprised and perplexed as they be have not drake with he usual presence of mind animated they courage and direct they motion order they by perpetually change they place to elude as much as they could the aim of they enemy and to defend they body with they target and instruct they by he own example to pick up and break the arrow as they fall which they do with so much diligence that the indian be soon in danger of be disarm then drake himself take the gun which oliver have so unsuccessfully attempt to make use of discharge it at the indian that first begin the fray and have kill the gunner aim it so happily that the hailshot with which it be load tear open he belly and force he to such terrible outcry that the indian though they number increase and many of they countryman show themselves from different part of the adjoining wood be too much terrify to renew the assault and suffer drake without molestation to withdraw he wounded friend who be hurt in he lung languish two day and then die be inter with he companion with the usual ceremony of a military funeral they stay here two month afterwards without receive any other injury from the native who find the danger to which they expose themselves by open hostility and not be able any more to surprise the vigilance of drake prefer they safety to revenge but drake have other enemy to conquer or escape far more formidable than these barbarian and insidious practice to obviate more artful and dangerous than the ambush of the indian for in this place be lay open a design form by one of the gentleman of the fleet not only to defeat the voyage but to murder the general this transaction be relate in so obscure and confuse a manner that it be difficult to form any judgment upon it the writer who give the largest account of it have suppress the name of the criminal which we learn from a more succinct narrative publish in a collection of travels near that time to have be thoma doughtie what be he inducement to attempt the destruction of he leader and the ruin of the expedition or what be he view if he design have succeed what measure he have hitherto take whom he have endeavor to corjupt with what art or what success we be nowhere tell the plot as the narrative assure we be lay before they departure from england and discover in its whole extent to drake himself in he garden at plymouth who nevertheless not only entertain the person so accuse as one of he company but this writer very particularly relate treated he with remarkable kindness and regard set he always at he own table and lodge he in the same cabin with himself nor do ever he discover the least suspicion of he intention till they arrive at this place but appear by the authority with which he invest he to consider he as one to whom in he absence he could most securely intrust the direction of he affair at length in this remote corner of the world he find out a design form against he life call together all he officer lay before they the evidence on which he ground the accusation and summon the criminal who full of all the horror of guilt and confound at so clear a detection of he whole scheme immediately confess he crime and acknowledge himself unworthy of longer life upon which the whole assembly consist of thirty person after have consider the affair with the attention which it require and hear all that could be urge in extenuation of he offence unanimously sign the sentence by which he be condemn to suffer death drake however unwilling as it seem to proceed to extreme severity offer he he choice either of be execute on the island or set ashore on the mainland or be send to england to be try before the council of which after a day 's consideration he choose the first allege the improbability of persuade any to leave the expedition for the sake of transport a criminal to england and the danger of he future state among savage and infidel he choice i believe few will approve : to be set ashore on the mainland be indeed only to be execute in a different manner for what mercy could be expect from the native so incensed but the most cruel and linger death but why he should not rather have request to be send to england it be not so easy to conceive in so long a voyage he might have find a thousand opportunity of escape perhaps with the connivance of he keeper whose resentment must probably in time have give way to compassion or at least by they negligence as it be easy to believe they would in time of ease and refreshment have remit they vigilance at least he would have gain longer life and to make death desirable seem not one of the effect of guilt however he be as it be related obstinately deaf to all persuasion and adhering to he first choice after have receive the communion and dine cheerfully with the general be execute in the afternoon with many proof of remorse but none of fear how far it be probable that drake after have be acquaint with this man 's design should admit he into he fleet and afterwards caress respect and trust he or that doughtie who be represent as a man of eminent ability should engage in so long and hazardous a voyage with no other view than that of defeat it be leave to the determination of the reader what design he could have form with any hope of success or to what action worthy of death he could have proceed without accomplice for none be mention be equally difficult to imagine nor on the other hand though the obscurity of the account and the remote place choose for the discovery of this wicked project seem to give some reason for suspicion do there appear any temptation from either hope fear or interest that might induce drake or any commander in he state to put to death a innocent man upon false pretence after the execution of this man the whole company either convinced of the justice of the proceeding or awed by the severity apply themselves without any murmur or appearance of discontent to the prosecution of the voyage and have break up another vessel and reduce the number of they ship to three they leave the port and on August the 20th enter the strait of magellan in which they struggle with contrary wind and the various danger to which the intricacy of that wind passage expose they till night and then enter a more open sea in which they discover a island with a burning mountain on the 24th they fall in with three more island to which drake give name and landing to take possession of they in the name of he sovereign find in the largest so prodigious a number of bird that they kill three thousand of they in one day this bird of which they know not the name be somewhat less than a wild goose without feather and cover with a kind of down unable to fly or rise from the ground but capable of run and swim with amazing celerity they feed on the sea and come to land only to rest at night or lay they egg which they deposit in hole like those of cony from these island to the south sea the strait become very crooked and narrow so that sometimes by the interposition of headland the passage seem shut up and the voyage entirely stop to double these cape be very difficult on account of the frequent alteration to be make in the course there be indeed as magellan observe many harbor but in most of they no bottom be to be find the land on both side rise into innumerable mountain the top of they be encircle with cloud and vapor which be congeal fall down in snow and increase they height by harden into ice which be never dissolve but the valley be nevertheless green fruitful and pleasant here drake find the strait in appearance shut up go in he boat to make further discovery and have find a passage towards the north be return to he ship but curiosity soon prevail upon he to stop for the sake of observe a canoe or boat with several native of the country in it he could not at a distance forbear admire the form of this little vessel which seem incline to a semicircle the stern and prow standing up and the body sink inward but much greater be he wonder when upon a nearer inspection he find it make only of the bark of tree sew together with thong of sealskin so artificially that scarcely any water enter the seam the people be well shape and paint like those which have be already describe on the land they have a hut build with pole and cover with skin in which they have water-vessel and other utensil make likewise of the bark of tree among these people they have a opportunity of remark what be frequently observable in savage country how natural sagacity and unwearied industry may supply the want of such manufacture or natural production as appear to we absolutely necessary for the support of life the inhabitant of these island be wholly stranger to iron and its use but instead of it make use of the shell of a muscle of prodigious size find upon they coast this they grind upon a stone to a edge which be so firm and solid that neither wood nor stone be able to resist it September 6 they enter the great south sea on which no english vessel have ever be navigate before and propose to have direct they course towards the line that they man who have suffer by the severity of the climate might recover they strength in a warmer latitude but they design be scarce form before they be frustrate for on sept 7 after a eclipse of the moon a storm arise so violent that it leave they little hope of survive it nor be its fury so dreadful as its continuance for it last with little intermission till October 28 fifty-two day during which time they be toss incessantly from one part of the ocean to another without any power of spread they sail or lie upon they anchor amidst shelve shore scatter rock and unknown island the tempest continually roar and the wave dash over they in this storm on the 30th of September the marigold command by captain thoma be separate from they on the 7th of October have enter a harbor where they hope for some intermission of they fatigue they be in a few hour force out to sea by a violent gust which break the cable at which time they lose sight of the elizabeth the viceadmiral whose crew as be afterwards discover wearied with labor and discourage by the prospect of future danger recover the strait on the next day and return by the same passage through which they come sail along the coast of brasil and on the 2nd of June in the year follow arrive at england from this bay they be drive southward to fifty-five degree where among some island they stay two day to the great refreshment of the crew but be again force into the main sea they be toss about with perpetual expectation of perish till soon after they again come to anchor near the same place where they find the native whom the continuance of the storm have probably reduce to equal distress rowing from one island to another and provide the necessaries of life it be perhaps a just observation that with regard to outward circumstance happiness and misery be equally diffuse through all state of human life in civilized country where regular policy have secure the necessaries of life ambition avarice and luxury find the mind at leisure for they reception and soon engage it in new pursuit pursuit that be to be carry on by incessant labor and whether vain or successful produce anxiety and contention among savage nation imaginary want find indeed no place but they strength be exhaust by necessary toil and they passion agitate not by contest about superiority affluence or precedence but by perpetual care for the present day and by fear of perish for want of food but for such reflection as these they have no time for have spend three day in supply themselves with wood and water they be by a new storm drive to the latitude of fifty-six degree where they behold the extremity of the american coast and the confluence of the atlantick and southern ocean here they arrive on the 28th of October and at last be bless with the sight of a calm sea have for almost two month endure such a storm as no traveller have give a account of and such as in that part of the world though accustom to hurricane they be before unacquainted with on the 30th of October they steer away towards the place appoint for the rendezvous of the fleet which be in thirty degree and on the next day discover two island so well stock with fowl that they victual they ship with they and then sail forward along the coast of peru till they come to thirty-seven degree where find neither of they ship nor any convenient port they come to anchor November the 25th at mucho a island inhabit by such indian as the cruelty of the spanish conqueror have drive from the continent to whom they apply for water and provision offer they in return such thing as they imagine most likely to please they the indian seem willing to and send two man forward towards the place appoint who about the middle of the way be suddenly attack by the indian and immediately slay nor be the rest of the company out of danger for behind the hinder they from either retire or make use of they weapon drake himself receive a arrow under he eye which pierce he almost to the brain and another in he head the danger of these wound be much providence that they all recover no reason could be assign for which the indian should attack they with so furious a spirit of malignity but that they mistake they for spaniard whose cruelty might very reasonably incite they to revenge whom they have drive by incessant persecution from they country waste immense tract of land by massacre and devastation on the afternoon of the same day they set be kindly treat be dismiss with present and inform as far as the english could make he understand what they chiefly want and what they be willing to give in return drake order he boat to attend he in he canoe and to set he safe on the land when he be ashore he direct they to wait till he return and meet some of he countryman give they such a account of he reception that within a few hour several ship at some place where they might commodiously build a pinnace which be of light burden might easily sail where the ship be in danger of be strand and at the same time might carry a sufficient force to resist the enemy and afford better accommodation than could be expect in the boat to this end on the 19th of December they enter a bay near cippo a town inhabit by spaniard who discover they he fall and in the sight of the english behead it then cut off the right hand and tear out the heart which they carry away have first command the indian to shoot they arrow all over the body the arrow of the indian be make of green wood for the immediate service of the day the spaniard with the fear that always harass oppressor forbid they to have any weapon when they do not want they present assistance leave this place they soon find a harbor more secure and convenient where they build they pinnace in which drake go to seek he companion but find the wind contrary he be oblige to return in landing in another place they find a spaniard drive eight peruvian sheep which be the beast of burden in that country each laden with a hundred pound weight of silver which they seize likewise and drive to they boat further along the coast lay some indian town from which the inhabitant repair to the ship on float make of sealskin blow full of wind two of which they fasten together and sit between they row with great swiftness and carry considerable burden they very readily trade for glass and such trifle with which the old and the young seem equally delighted arrive at mormorena on the 26th of January drake invite the spaniard to traffick with he which they agree to and supply he with necessaries sell to he among other provision some of those sheep which have be mention whose bulk be equal to that of a cow and whose strength be such that one of they can carry three tall man upon he back they neck be like a camel 's and they head like those of we sheep they be the most useful animal of this country not only afford excellent fleece and wholesome flesh but serve as carriage over rock and mountain where no other beast can travel for they foot be of a peculiar form which enable they to tread firm in the most steep and slippery place on all this coast the whole soil be so impregnate with silver that five ounce may be separate from a hundred pound weight of common earth still coast in hope of meet they friend they anchor on the 7th of February before aria where they take two bark with about eight hundred pound weight of silver and pursue they course seize another vessel laden with linen on the 15th of February 1578 they arrive at lima and enter the harbor without resistance though thirty ship be station there of which seventeen be equip for they voyage and many of they be represent in the narrative as vessel of considerable force so that they security seem to have consist not in they strength but in they reputation which have so intimidate the spaniard that the sight of they own superiority could not rouse they to opposition instance of such panick terror be to be meet with in other relation but as they be for the most part quickly dissipate by reason and reflection a wise commander will rarely find he hope of success on they and perhaps on this occasion the spaniard scarcely deserve a severer censure for they cowardice than drake for he
